# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Summary

I've found and documented **exponential backoff with retry implementations** across all three major Go repositories:

### **Kubernetes (8 files)**
- Core backoff implementation in `wait` package with `ExponentialBackoff()` and `ExponentialBackoffWithContext()`
- Retry utilities using `OnError()` wrapper
- Operation-level backoff in goroutine map and volume operations
- Webhook retry mechanisms

### **Grafana (4 files)**
- Git repository retrier using external `nanogit/retry` package with `ExponentialBackoffRetrier`
- Alert scheduling retrier implementing exponential backoff from 100ms doubling to 5s max
- Resource interface retry client using Kubernetes' wait package
- Utility retry functions with configurable delays

### **Prometheus (4 files)**
- Remote write backoff in `QueueManager.sendWriteRequestWithBackoff()` with configurable min/max delays
- `RecoverableError` type for wrapping retry-able failures
- HTTP client retry logic with Retry-After header support
- TSDB compaction retry with exponential backoff

The answer file includes 16 relevant files, 18 key symbols/functions, and a detailed narrative explaining how exponential backoff is implemented and used across these projects, including common patterns like multiplier strategies (2x), jitter, context awareness, and error classification.

The function:\\n   - Starts with `t.cfg.MinBackoff` (default 30ms)\\n   - Doubles the backoff on each failure: `backoff = min(sleepDuration*2, t.cfg.MaxBackoff)`\\n   - Caps at `t.cfg.MaxBackoff` (default 5 seconds)\\n   - Supports Retry-After header from remote endpoints\\n   - Disables resharding during active backoffs to avoid amplifying problems\\n\\n2. **HTTP Client Integration**: `storage/remote/client.go` defines `RecoverableError` struct (line 258) that wraps errors with `retryAfter` duration for fine-grained backoff control. The `Store()` function (line 265) returns `RecoverableError` for network errors and HTTP 5xx responses, enabling the queue manager to apply backoff.\\n\\n3. **Configuration**: `config/config.go` defines `RemoteWriteConfig` (line 1555) with `MinBackoff` and `MaxBackoff` fields of type `model.Duration`, allowing users to configure retry behavior per remote write endpoint.\\n\\n4. **TSDB Compaction**: `tsdb/db.go` (line 1231) implements an exponential backoff pattern for database compaction failures using a simple doubling strategy.\\n\\n### Cross-Repository Pattern Analysis\\n\\nAll three projects implement exponential backoff following common principles:\\n- **Initial delay**: Small initial wait (Kubernetes: varies by use case, Grafana: 100ms, Prometheus: 30ms)\\n- **Multiplier strategy**: Consistent doubling (2x) of the delay after each failure\\n- **Maximum cap**: Upper limit to prevent infinite delays (Kubernetes goroutine: 2m2s, Grafana git: 5s, Prometheus: 5s)\\n- **Jitter**: Random factor added to prevent thundering herd (explicit in Kubernetes/Grafana, implicit in Prometheus)\\n- **Context awareness**: Support for context cancellation and deadlines\\n- **Error classification**: Distinction between recoverable and non-recoverable errors\\n\\nThe implementations reflect the different use cases: Kubernetes focuses on API operations and pod/volume management, Grafana on git operations and alerting, and Prometheus specifically on remote write reliability.\\n\"\n}\n",
